<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott Laboratories and Subsidiaries</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial
Statements</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">September&nbsp;30, 2005</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(Unaudited)</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note
1 &#150; Basis of Presentation</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
accompanying unaudited, condensed consolidated financial statements have been prepared
pursuant to rules&nbsp;and regulations of the Securities and Exchange
Commission and, therefore, do not include all information and footnote
disclosures normally included in audited financial statements.&#160; However, in the opinion of management, all
adjustments necessary to present fairly the results of operations, financial
position and cash flows have been made.&#160;
It is suggested that these statements be read in conjunction with the
financial statements included in Abbott&#146;s Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K for
the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2004.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note
2 &#150; Spin-off of Hospira</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On
April&nbsp;12, 2004, Abbott&#146;s board of directors declared a special dividend
distribution of all of the outstanding shares of common stock of Hospira,&nbsp;Inc.&#160; For every 10 Abbott common shares held at the
close of business on April&nbsp;22, 2004, Abbott shareholders received one
share of Hospira stock on April&nbsp;30, 2004.&#160;
Hospira included the operations relating to the manufacture and sale of
hospital products including specialty injectable pharmaceuticals, medication
delivery systems and critical care devices and injectable pharmaceutical
contract manufacturing.&#160; Hospira included
Abbott&#146;s Hospital products segment, after that segment&#146;s reorganization on January&nbsp;1,
2004, and portions of Abbott&#146;s International segment.&#160; The income and cash flows of Hospira and the
direct transaction costs of the spin-off have been presented as discontinued
operations in the Condensed Consolidated Statement of Earnings and Condensed Consolidated
Statement of Cash Flows.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
legal transfer of certain operations and assets (net of liabilities) outside
the United States is expected to occur in 2005 and 2006.&#160; Approximately half of these operations are
expected to be transferred to Hospira in 2005 with the remaining operations
transferring in the first half of 2006.&#160;
As of September&nbsp;30, 2005, 48 percent of these operations have been
transferred to Hospira.&#160; These operations
and assets are used in the conduct of Hospira&#146;s international business and
Hospira is subject to the risks and entitled to the benefits generated by these
operations and assets.&#160; These assets and
liabilities have been presented as held for sale in the Condensed Consolidated
Balance Sheet.&#160; The assets and
liabilities held for sale consist primarily of inventories, trade accounts
receivable, equipment and trade accounts payable, salaries and other accruals.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Summarized
financial information for discontinued operations is as follows: <i><font style="font-style:italic;">(dollars in thousands)</font></i></font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Supplemental
Cash Flow Information &#150; Other, net in Net Cash From Operating Activities of Continuing
Operations for 2005 includes the effects of contributions to the main domestic
defined benefit plan of $641,000 and to the post-employment medical and dental
plans of $140,000.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note
4 &#150; Taxes on Earnings</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Taxes
on earnings reflect the estimated annual effective rates and for the first nine
months 2005 include additional income taxes of approximately $52 million for
remittances of foreign earnings of approximately $600 million in connection
with the American Jobs Creation Act of 2004.&#160;
In February&nbsp;2005, management concluded that it would remit these
earnings in 2005.&#160; In October&nbsp;2005,
Abbott management concluded that it would remit an additional $3.7 billion of
foreign earnings in 2005.&#160; The additional
income tax expense required for the $3.7 billion is approximately $220 million
and is expected to be recorded in the fourth quarter of 2005.&#160; 2004 includes the effects of charges for
acquired in-process research and development and for other non-tax deductible items.&#160; The effective tax rates, excluding the effect
of these 2005 and 2004 items, are less than the statutory U.S. federal income
tax rate principally due to the domestic dividend exclusion and the benefit of
lower statutory tax rates and tax exemptions in several taxing jurisdictions.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note
5 &#150; Litigation and Environmental Matters</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As
of December&nbsp;31, 2004, there were several lawsuits pending in connection
with the sales of<i><font style="font-style:italic;"> Hytrin</font></i>. These
suits alleged that Abbott violated state or federal antitrust laws and, in some
cases, unfair competition laws by signing patent settlement agreements with
Geneva Pharmaceuticals,&nbsp;Inc. and Zenith Laboratories,&nbsp;Inc. in 1998.
Those agreements related to pending patent infringement lawsuits between Abbott
and the two companies.&#160; In the second
quarter of 2005, the court approved settlements with the majority of the
plaintiffs in the aggregate amount of $90 million which was previously
reserved.&#160; The claims of the remaining
plaintiffs are not material and are reserved for by Abbott.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott
has been identified as a potentially responsible party for investigation and
cleanup costs at a number of locations in the United States and Puerto Rico
under federal and state remediation laws and is investigating potential
contamination at a number of company-owned locations. Abbott has recorded an
estimated cleanup cost for each site for which management believes Abbott has a
probable loss exposure. No individual site cleanup exposure is expected to
exceed $3&nbsp;million, and the aggregate cleanup exposure is not expected to
exceed $20&nbsp;million.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Within
the next year, legal proceedings may occur that may result in a change in the
estimated reserves recorded by Abbott.&nbsp; For its legal proceedings and
environmental exposures, including those discussed in this note and in Note 6,
Abbott estimates the range of possible loss to be from approximately $25
million to $110 million.&#160; Reserves of
approximately $45 million have been recorded at September&nbsp;30, 2005 for
these proceedings and exposures.&nbsp; These reserves represent management&#146;s
best estimate of probable loss, except for one which is recorded at the
minimum, as defined by Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;5, &#147;Accounting
for Contingencies.&#148;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">While
it is not feasible to predict the outcome of all such proceedings and exposures
with certainty, management believes that their ultimate disposition should not
have a material adverse effect on Abbott&#146;s financial position, cash flows, or
results of operations.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">6</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note
6 &#150; TAP Pharmaceutical Products Inc.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As
of December&nbsp;31, 2004, TAP Pharmaceutical Products&nbsp;Inc. (TAP) and
Abbott were named as defendants in several lawsuits alleging violations of
various state or federal laws in connection with TAP&#146;s marketing and pricing of
<i><font style="font-style:italic;">Lupron</font></i>. In the second quarter of
2005, the court approved settlements with the majority of the plaintiffs in the
aggregate amount of $150 million which was previously reserved.&#160; The claims of the remaining plaintiffs are
not material and are reserved for by TAP.&#160;
Abbott&#146;s portion of TAP&#146;s remaining reserve is included in the reserve
amounts and range in Note 5 above.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Within
the next year, legal proceedings may occur that may result in a change in the
estimated reserves recorded by TAP. While it is not feasible to predict the
outcome of such pending claims, proceedings, and investigations with certainty,
management is of the opinion that their ultimate disposition should not have a
material adverse effect on Abbott&#146;s financial position, cash flows, or results
of operations.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note
7 &#150; Post-Employment Benefits</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(dollars in millions)</font></i></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Retirement plans consist of defined benefit, defined contribution, and
medical and dental plans.&#160; Net cost
recognized in continuing operations for the nine months ended September&nbsp;30
for Abbott&#146;s major defined benefit plans and post-employment medical and dental
benefit plans is as follows:</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott funds its domestic defined benefit plans according to IRS
funding limitations.&#160; In the first nine
months of 2005, $641 was contributed to the main domestic defined benefit plan
and $140 was contributed to the post-employment medical and dental benefit
plans. In the first nine months of 2004, $295 was contributed to the main
domestic defined benefit plan.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note
9 &#150; Segment Information <i><font style="font-style:italic;">(dollars in
millions)</font></i></font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Revenue Segments</font></i>&#151; Abbott&#146;s principal business is the
discovery, development, manufacture and sale of a broad line of health care
products.&#160; Abbott&#146;s products are
generally sold directly to retailers, wholesalers, hospitals, health care
facilities, laboratories, physicians&#146; offices and government agencies
throughout the world.&#160; Abbott&#146;s
reportable segments are as follows:</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Pharmaceutical Products</font></i>&#151; U.S. sales of a broad line of
pharmaceuticals.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Diagnostic Products</font></i>&#151; Worldwide sales of diagnostic systems and
tests for blood banks, hospitals, consumers, commercial laboratories and
alternate-care testing sites.&#160; For
segment reporting purposes, four diagnostic divisions are aggregated and
reported as the Diagnostic products segment.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Ross Products</font></i>&#151; Primarily U.S. sales of a broad line of adult
and pediatric nutritional products, pediatric pharmaceuticals and consumer
products.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">International</font></i>&#151; Non-U.S. sales of Abbott&#146;s pharmaceutical
and nutritional products. Products sold by International are manufactured in
domestic and international manufacturing locations.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott&#146;s underlying accounting records are maintained on a legal entity
basis for government and public reporting requirements. Segment disclosures are
on a performance basis consistent with internal management reporting.&#160; Intersegment transfers of inventory are
recorded at standard cost and are not a measure of segment operating
earnings.&#160; The cost of some corporate
functions and the cost of certain employee benefits are sold to segments at
predetermined rates that approximate cost.&#160;
Remaining costs, if any, are not allocated to segments.&#160; Substantially all intangible assets and
related amortization from business acquisitions are not allocated to
segments.&#160; The following segment
information has been prepared in accordance with the internal accounting
policies of Abbott, as described above, and are not presented in accordance
with generally accepted accounting principles applied to the consolidated
financial statements.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">8</font></p>

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(a)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Net sales and operating earnings for the Ross segment for the third
quarter and first nine months 2005 includes $70 from a revised agreement for
the U.S. promotion of <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Synagis</font></i>.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(b)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Other, net for the third quarter of 2005 includes $203 for
restructuring and impairment charges as discussed in Note 14 and an increase in
a bad debt reserve of $58 associated with an unfavorable court ruling.&#160; Other, net for the first nine months of 2005
includes $231 for restructuring and impairment charges as discussed in Note 14
and an increase in a bad debt reserve of $58 associated with an unfavorable
court ruling.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note
10 &#150; Business Combinations and Technology Acquisitions</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
the third quarter of 2005, Abbott acquired the remaining interest in a small
medical products company that was previously accounted for under the equity
method of accounting.&#160; The cash purchase
price was approximately $10 million.&#160;
Acquisition accounting resulted in the recording of non-tax deductible
goodwill of approximately $67 million, intangible assets of approximately $22
million and a charge of approximately $2 million for acquired in-process
research and development.&#160; In addition,
Abbott acquired a less than 50 percent equity interest in a small medical
products company for approximately $15 million in cash, resulting in a charge
to acquired in-process research and development of approximately $15 million.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
April&nbsp;2004, Abbott acquired TheraSense,&nbsp;Inc., a leader in the
development, manufacturing and marketing of blood glucose self-monitoring
systems, for approximately $1.2 billion in cash.&#160; Abbott also acquired certain other product
technologies for approximately $352 million.&#160;
These acquisitions resulted in a charge of $164 million for acquired
in-process research and development, intangible assets of approximately $912
million, non-tax deductible goodwill of approximately $623 million and deferred
income taxes of approximately $241 million.&#160;
Acquired intangible assets, primarily product technology, are amortized
over 9 to 17 years (average of approximately 13 years).&#160; In January&nbsp;2004, Abbott acquired i-STAT
Corporation, a manufacturer of point-of-care diagnostic products for blood
analysis, for approximately $394 million in cash.&#160; In the first quarter of 2004, Abbott recorded
a charge of approximately $60 million for acquired in-process research and
development, intangible assets of approximately $263 million, non-tax
deductible goodwill of approximately $109 million and deferred income taxes of
approximately $105 million.&#160; Acquired
intangible assets, primarily product technology, are amortized over 7 to 18
years (average of approximately 17 years).</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Had
these acquisitions taken place on January&nbsp;1 of the previous year,
consolidated sales and income would not have been significantly different from
reported amounts.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">9</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<div>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note
11 &#150; Incentive Stock Programs</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott
measures compensation cost using the intrinsic value-based method of accounting
for stock options and replacement stock options granted to employees.&#160; Had compensation cost been determined using a
fair market value-based accounting method, pro&nbsp;forma net earnings (<i><font style="font-style:italic;">in millions</font></i>) and earnings per share (EPS)
amounts would have been as shown in the table below.&#160; Effective in the first quarter 2005, the
calculation of pro forma compensation expense was modified to reflect a shorter
vesting period for employees who are retirement eligible or who will be
retirement eligible during the normal vesting period. Approximately 40 to 45
percent of the annual net cost of stock options granted will typically be
recognized in the first quarter due to the timing of stock option grants.&#160; The effect of this change has an immaterial
effect on the annual pro forma compensation expense.&#160; The quarterly pro forma compensation cost and
EPS amounts for 2004 have been adjusted to reflect this change.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
above information was derived using Statement of Financial Accounting Standards
(SFAS) No.&nbsp;123 and the Black-Scholes valuation model.&#160; In December&nbsp;2004, the Financial
Accounting Standards Board issued SFAS No.&nbsp;123 (revised 2004), &#147;Share-Based
Payment.&#148;&#160; This standard required
companies to expense employee stock options beginning no later than July&nbsp;1,
2005.&#160; On April&nbsp;14, 2005, the
Securities and Exchange Commission announced that companies may implement SFAS No.&nbsp;123
(revised 2004) at the beginning of their next fiscal year that begins after June&nbsp;15,
2005.&#160; Abbott expects to adopt the
revised rules&nbsp;on January&nbsp;1, 2006.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note
12 &#150; Equity Method Investments</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(dollars in millions)</font></i></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott&#146;s 50 percent-owned joint venture, TAP Pharmaceutical
Products&nbsp;Inc. (TAP), is accounted for under the equity method of
accounting.&#160; Summarized financial
information for TAP is as follows:</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note&nbsp;13&nbsp;&#150;
Goodwill and Intangible Assets</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(dollars in millions)</font></i></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott
recorded goodwill of approximately $67 related to the acquisition of a medical
device company in the third quarter of 2005. Abbott also recorded goodwill of
approximately $834 related to the acquisitions of TheraSense in the second
quarter of 2004 and<br>
i-STAT in the first quarter of 2004.&#160;
Foreign currency translation adjustments (decreased) increased goodwill
in the first nine months of 2005 and 2004 by approximately ($350) and $14,
respectively and approximately $81 was transferred to Hospira.&#160; There were no other reductions of goodwill
relating to impairments or disposal of all or a portion of a business.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
gross amount of amortizable intangible assets, primarily product rights and
technology, was $6,548 as of September&nbsp;30, 2005 and $6,622 as of December&nbsp;31,
2004, and accumulated amortization was $1,888 as of September&nbsp;30, 2005 and
$1,468 as of December&nbsp;31, 2004.&#160;
Intangible assets with indefinite lives are not significant.&#160; The estimated annual amortization expense for
intangible assets is $491 in 2005, $483 in 2006, $467 in 2007, $449 in 2008,
and $443 in 2009.&#160; Intangible assets are
amortized primarily on a straight-line basis over 4 to 25&nbsp;years (average
13&nbsp;years).</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">11</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<div>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note
14 &#150; Restructuring Plans</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(dollars in millions)</font></i></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
2005, Abbott management approved plans to realign its global manufacturing
operations and selected international commercial operations.&#160; In the second and third quarters of 2005,
Abbott recorded pretax charges against earnings of approximately $229
reflecting the impairment of manufacturing facilities and other assets,
employee severance and other related charges.&#160;
Approximately $175 is classified as cost of products sold, $5 as
research and development and $49 as selling, general and administrative.&#160; An additional $2 was incurred in the third
quarter relating to these restructurings, primarily for accelerated
depreciation.&#160; As a result of product
re-registration timelines required under manufacturing regulations in a number
of countries, this manufacturing realignment will continue into 2007.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
following summarizes the restructuring activity for the global pharmaceutical
manufacturing operations restructuring:</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott
expects to incur up to an additional $190 in future periods for restructuring
plans, primarily for accelerated depreciation and plant and equipment
dispositions.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note
15 &#150; Subsequent Event</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
October&nbsp;2005, Abbott announced that it had reached agreement with
Cambridge Antibody Technologies (CAT) whereby Abbott will pay fixed and
revenue-based royalties to CAT.&#160; The
present value of the fixed portion of the royalties, amounting to approximately
$270 million, will be recorded as an amortizable intangible asset in the fourth
quarter of 2005.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(a)
Percentage changes are based on unrounded numbers.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Worldwide
sales for the third quarter and nine months 2005 reflect primarily unit growth
and the positive effect of the relatively weaker U.S. dollar.&#160; The relatively weaker U.S. dollar increased
third quarter and first nine months 2005 consolidated net sales 1.1&nbsp;percent
and 2.0 percent respectively, and increased Total International sales 2.6
percent and 4.6 percent over the third quarter and first nine months 2004.&#160; In addition, the effect of the relatively
weaker U.S. dollar increased third quarter and first nine months 2005 sales in
the Diagnostic products segment by 1.6 percent and 3.2 percent, respectively,
and International segment sales by 2.6 percent and 4.5 percent,
respectively.&#160; Sales for the Ross segment
were favorably impacted in 2005 by the acquisition of EAS in the fourth quarter
of 2004 and by incremental revenue of $70 million, recorded in the third
quarter of 2005, from a revised agreement for the U.S. promotion of <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Synagis</font></i>.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#160;(a)
Percentage changes are versus the prior year and are based on unrounded
numbers.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Increased
sales volume of <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Mobic</font></i> in 2005
favorably impacted the Primary Care product sales of the Pharmaceutical
products segment, and increased sales volume of <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Humira</font></i> favorably impacted Specialty product sales in 2005
and 2004. U.S. sales of <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Synthroid</font></i>,
which is now subject to generic competition,<i><font style="font-style:italic;"> </font></i>were $358 million and $496 million in the first nine months of 2005
and 2004, respectively.&#160; Increased sales
volume of <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Humira</font></i> also favorably
impacted Other Pharmaceuticals sales in the International segment.&#160; Worldwide sales of <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Humira</font></i> totaled $959 million in the first nine months 2005
and are forecasted to be more than $1.3 billion for the full year 2005.&#160; Diagnostics and International segment product
sales were favorably impacted in 2005 and 2004 by the effect of the relatively
weaker U.S. dollar.&#160; Diabetes Care
product sales for the Diagnostic segment were favorably impacted by the
acquisition of TheraSense in the second quarter of 2004.<b><font style="font-weight:bold;">&#160; </font></b>Adult
Nutritionals product sales for the Ross products segment were favorably
impacted by the acquisition of EAS in the fourth quarter of 2004 and Pediatric
Nutritional product sales were unfavorably impacted in 2005 due to lower sales
of <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Similac</font></i>.&#160; In the third quarter of 2005, Baxter
International received a court ruling that its proposed generic sevoflurane
product does not infringe Abbott&#146;s patents.&#160;
Abbott has appealed. &#160;Baxter is
prohibited from marketing their product in the U.S. or exporting outside the
U.S. until after December&nbsp;10, 2005, as a result of a previous Alternative
Dispute Resolution between the parties.&#160;
U.S. and international sales of sevoflurane were $246 million and $395
million, respectively, for the first nine months of 2005.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
gross profit margin was 50.3 percent for the third quarter 2005, compared to
54.8 percent for the third quarter 2004.&#160;
First nine months 2005 gross profit margin was 51.9 percent, compared to
55.4 percent for the first nine months 2004.&#160;
The decrease in the gross profit margins was due to unfavorable product
mix, primarily as a result of increased sales of Boehringer Ingelheim products
that have lower margins than other products in the Pharmaceutical products
segment.&#160; Restructuring charges,
discussed below, reduced the gross profit margin in the third quarter and first
nine months 2005 by 2.9 and 1.1 percentage points, respectively.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">14</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='14',FILE='C:\JMS\sgopala\05-18480-1\task636254\18480-1-ba.htm',USER='sgopaladas',CD='Nov  3 00:02 2005' -->


<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
2005, Abbott and Boehringer Ingelheim amended the terms of the agreement under
which Abbott distributes certain Boehringer Ingelheim products.&#160; The amended terms will take effect on January&nbsp;1,
2006.&#160; Abbott will no longer distribute,
or record sales for the Boehringer Ingelheim products, but will co-promote one
product, <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Micardis</font></i>, through March&nbsp;31,
2006, and will receive residual commissions on Boehringer Ingelheim&#146;s sales of
the three products. The amount of pretax income under the revised arrangement
will be the same as expected under the previous agreement. Net sales of
Boehringer Ingelheim products for the first nine months of 2005 were
approximately $1.7 billion.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Research
and development expenses increased 14.6 percent in the third quarter 2005 and
7.9 percent for the first nine months 2005, respectively, over comparable 2004
periods.&#160; These increases were due, in
part, to increased spending to support late-stage pharmaceutical pipeline
programs, including follow-on indications for <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Humira</font></i>,
and<i><font style="font-style:italic;"> </font></i>on clinical programs in the
vascular business.&#160; The majority of
research and development expenditures are concentrated on pharmaceutical
products<b><font style="font-weight:bold;">.</font></b></font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Selling,
general and administrative expenses for the third quarter and first nine months
2005 increased 23.2 percent and 14.6 percent, respectively, over the comparable
2004 periods.&#160; The restructuring charges
discussed below and an increase in a bad debt reserve associated with an
unfavorable court ruling increased the percent change from 2004 by 8.9 and 3.1
percentage points in the third quarter and first nine months 2005,
respectively.&#160; These increases were also
due to increased selling and marketing support for new and existing products,
including commercial activities related to sales force expansion and product
launches including Abbott&#146;s carotid stent and new <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Humira</font></i><i><font style="font-style:italic;"> </font></i>indications.&#160; These increases also reflect the effects of
the acquisitions of TheraSense in the second quarter of 2004 and EAS in the
fourth quarter of 2004.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott&#146;s
income from the TAP Pharmaceutical Products Inc. joint venture for the third
quarter and first nine months of 2004 was adversely affected by approximately
$40 million as a result of an agreement with plaintiffs to settle litigation.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Restructurings</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(dollars in millions)</font></i></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
2005, Abbott management approved plans to realign its global manufacturing
operations and selected international commercial operations.&#160; In the second and third quarters of 2005,
Abbott recorded pretax charges against earnings of approximately $229
reflecting the impairment of manufacturing facilities and other assets,
employee severance and other related charges.&#160;
Approximately $175 is classified as cost of products sold, $5 as
research and development and $49 as selling, general and administrative.&#160; An additional $2 was incurred in the third
quarter relating to these restructurings, primarily for accelerated
depreciation.&#160; As a result of product
re-registration timelines required under manufacturing regulations in a number
of countries, this manufacturing realignment will continue into 2007.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#160;The following summarizes the restructuring
activity for the global pharmaceutical manufacturing operations restructuring:</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott
expects to incur up to an additional $190 in future periods for restructuring
plans, primarily for accelerated depreciation and plant and equipment
dispositions.</font></p>

<div>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Subsequent Event</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
October&nbsp;2005, Abbott announced that it had reached agreement with
Cambridge Antibody Technologies (CAT) whereby Abbott will pay fixed and
revenue-based royalties to CAT.&#160; The
present value of the fixed portion of the royalties, amounting to approximately
$270 million, will be recorded as an amortizable intangible asset in the fourth
quarter of 2005.&#160; The fixed and variable
royalties under the revised agreement are expected to result in lower expense
compared to the prior agreement.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Spin-off of Hospira</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On
April&nbsp;12, 2004, Abbott&#146;s board of directors declared a special dividend
distribution of all of the outstanding shares of common stock of Hospira,&nbsp;Inc.&#160; For every 10 Abbott common shares held at the
close of business on April&nbsp;22, 2004, Abbott shareholders received one
share of Hospira stock on April&nbsp;30, 2004.&#160;
Hospira included the operations relating to the manufacture and sale of
hospital products including specialty injectable pharmaceuticals, medication
delivery systems and critical care devices and injectable pharmaceutical
contract manufacturing.&#160; Hospira included
Abbott&#146;s Hospital products segment, after that segment&#146;s reorganization on January&nbsp;1,
2004, and portions of Abbott&#146;s International segment.&#160; The income and cash flows of Hospira and the
direct transaction costs of the spin-off have been presented as discontinued
operations in the Condensed Consolidated Statement of Earnings and Condensed
Consolidated Statement of Cash Flows.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
legal transfer of certain operations and assets (net of liabilities) outside
the United States is expected to occur in 2005 and 2006.&#160; Approximately half of these operations are
expected to be transferred to Hospira in 2005 with the remaining operations
transferring in the first half of 2006.&#160;
As of September&nbsp;30, 2005, 48 percent of the operations have been
transferred to Hospira.&#160; These operations
and assets are used in the conduct of Hospira&#146;s international business and
Hospira is subject to the risks and entitled to the benefits generated by these
operations and assets.&#160; These assets and
liabilities have been presented as held for sale in the Condensed Consolidated
Balance Sheet.&#160; The assets and
liabilities held for sale consist primarily of inventories, trade accounts
receivable, equipment and trade accounts payable, salaries and other accruals.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Interest Expense</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net
interest expense increased in both the third quarter and first nine months of
2005 due to the impact of higher interest rates on debt levels, partially
offset by higher interest income.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Taxes on Earnings</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Taxes
on earnings reflect the estimated annual effective rates and for the first nine
months 2005 include additional income taxes of approximately $52 million for
remittances of foreign earnings of approximately $600 million in connection
with the American Jobs Creation Act of 2004.&#160;
In February&nbsp;2005, management concluded that it would remit these
earnings in 2005.&#160; In October&nbsp;2005,
Abbott management concluded that it would remit an additional $3.7 billion of
foreign earnings in 2005.&#160; The additional
income tax expense required for the $3.7 billion is approximately $220 million
and is expected to be recorded in the fourth quarter of 2005.&#160; The effect of the increased income taxes on
the remittance of foreign earnings was to increase the first nine months 2005
effective tax rate by approximately 1.6 percentage points.&#160; 2004 also includes the effects of charges for
acquired in-process research and development and other non-tax deductible
items.&#160; The effective tax rates,
excluding the effect of the 2005 and 2004 items, are less than the statutory
U.S. federal income tax rate principally due to the domestic dividend exclusion
and the benefit of lower statutory tax rates and tax exemptions in several
taxing jurisdictions.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">16</font></p>

<div>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Business Combinations and Technology Acquisitions</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
the third quarter of 2005, Abbott acquired the remaining interest in a small
medical products company that was previously accounted for under the equity
method of accounting.&#160; The cash purchase
price was approximately $10 million.&#160;
Acquisition accounting resulted in the recording of non-tax deductible
goodwill of approximately $67 million, intangible assets of approximately $22
million and a charge of approximately $2 million for acquired in-process
research and development.&#160; In addition,
Abbott acquired a less than 50 percent equity interest in a small medical
products company for approximately $15 million in cash, resulting in a charge
to acquired in-process research and development of approximately $15 million.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
April&nbsp;2004, Abbott acquired TheraSense,&nbsp;Inc., a leader in the
development, manufacturing and marketing of blood glucose self-monitoring
systems, for approximately $1.2 billion in cash.&#160; Abbott also acquired certain other product
technologies for approximately $352 million.&#160;
These acquisitions resulted in a charge of $164 million for acquired
in-process research and development, intangible assets of approximately $912
million, non-tax deductible goodwill of approximately $623 million and deferred
income taxes of approximately $241 million.&#160;
Acquired intangible assets, primarily product technology, are amortized
over 9 to 17 years (average of approximately 13 years).&#160; In January&nbsp;2004, Abbott acquired i-STAT
Corporation, a manufacturer of point-of-care diagnostic products for blood
analysis, for approximately $394 million in cash.&#160; In the first quarter of 2004, Abbott recorded
a charge of approximately $60 million for acquired in-process research and
development, intangible assets of approximately $263 million, non-tax
deductible goodwill of approximately $109 million and deferred income taxes of
approximately $105 million.&#160; Acquired
intangible assets, primarily product technology, are amortized over 7 to 18
years (average of approximately 17 years).</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Had
these acquisitions taken place on January&nbsp;1 of the previous year,
consolidated sales and income would not have been significantly different from
reported amounts.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Liquidity and Capital Resources at September&nbsp;30, 2005 Compared
with December&nbsp;31, 2004</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net
cash from operating activities of continuing operations for the first nine
months 2005 totaled $3.7 billion. Abbott expects annual cash flow from
operating activities to continue to exceed Abbott&#146;s capital expenditures and
cash dividends.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">At
September&nbsp;30, 2005, Abbott had working capital of approximately $2.2
billion compared to working capital of approximately $3.9&nbsp;billion at December&nbsp;31,
2004.&#160; The decrease in working capital is
due to an increase in the current portion of long-term debt.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">At
September&nbsp;30, 2005, Abbott&#146;s long-term debt rating was AA by Standard&nbsp;&amp;
Poor&#146;s Corporation and A1 by Moody&#146;s Investors Service. Abbott has readily
available financial resources, including unused lines of credit of $3.0
billion, which support commercial paper borrowing arrangements.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
October&nbsp;2004, the board of directors authorized the purchase of 50 million
shares of Abbott&#146;s common stock from time to time and no shares were purchased
under this authorization in 2004.&#160; During
the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, Abbott purchased approximately
17.4<b><font style="font-weight:bold;"> </font></b>million of its common shares
under this authorization at a cost of approximately $802 million.&#160; In the nine months ended September&nbsp;30,
2004, Abbott purchased approximately 11.7 million of its common shares at a
cost of approximately $500&nbsp;million under a prior authorization.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Under
a registration statement filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission in September&nbsp;2003,
Abbott issued $1.5 billion of long-term debt in the first quarter of 2004 that
matures in 2009 through 2014 with interest rates ranging from 3.5 percent to 4.35&nbsp;percent.&#160; Proceeds from this debt were used to fund the
acquisition of TheraSense in the second quarter of 2004 and to pay down
domestic commercial paper borrowings.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">17</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Recently Issued Accounting Standards</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
May&nbsp;2005, the Financial Accounting Standards Board issued Statement of
Financial Accounting Standards&#160; (SFAS) No.&nbsp;154,
&#147;Accounting Changes and Error Corrections.&#148;&#160;
This statement generally requires retrospective application to prior
periods&#146; financial statements of voluntary changes in accounting
principles.&#160; Under the prior rules,
changes in accounting principles were generally recognized by including in net
income of the period of the change the cumulative effect of changing to the new
accounting principle.&#160; This statement
does not change the previous guidance for reporting the correction of an error
in previously issued financial statements, change in accounting estimate or
justification of a change in accounting principle on the basis of
preferability.&#160; This statement is
effective for accounting changes made in fiscal years beginning after December&nbsp;15,
2005.&#160; Adoption of the provisions of the
Statement is not expected to have a material affect on the results of
operations or financial position of Abbott.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
December&nbsp;2004, the Financial Accounting Standards Board issued a revised
Statement of Financial Accounting Standards&#160;
(SFAS) No.&nbsp;123 (revised 2004), &#147;Share-Based Payment.&#148;&#160;&#160; This standard required companies to expense
employee stock options beginning no later than July&nbsp;1, 2005.&#160; On April&nbsp;14, 2005, the Securities and
Exchange Commission announced that companies may implement SFAS No.&nbsp;123
(revised 2004) at the beginning of their next fiscal year that begins after June&nbsp;15,
2005.&#160; Abbott expects to adopt the
revised rules&nbsp;on January&nbsp;1, 2006.&#160;
Abbott expects that stock compensation expense under the rules&nbsp;would
reduce reported diluted earnings per share by approximately 14 cents in
2005.&#160; The effect of adopting the new
standard on diluted earnings per share in future periods is dependent on the
number of options granted in the future, the terms of those awards and their
fair values.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Legislative Issues</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott&#146;s
primary markets are highly competitive and subject to substantial government
regulation.&#160; Abbott expects debate to
continue at both the federal and the state levels over the availability, method
of delivery, and payment for health care products and services.&#160; Abbott believes that if legislation is
enacted, it could have the effect of reducing prices, or reducing the rate of
price increases for health care products and services.&#160; International operations are also subject to
a significant degree of government regulation.&#160;
It is not possible to predict the extent to which Abbott or the health
care industry in general might be adversely affected by these factors in the
future.&#160; A more complete discussion
of&nbsp;these factors is contained in Item 1, Business, in the Annual Report on
Form&nbsp;10-K, which is available upon request.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of 1995 &#151; A Caution Concerning
Forward-Looking Statements</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Under
the safe harbor provisions of the Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of
1995, Abbott cautions investors that any forward-looking statements or
projections made by Abbott, including those made in this document, are subject
to risks and uncertainties that may cause actual results to differ materially
from those projected. Economic, competitive, governmental, technological and
other factors that may affect Abbott&#146;s operations are discussed in Exhibit&nbsp;99.1
to the Quarterly Report on Form&nbsp;10-Q for the quarter ended March&nbsp;31,
2005.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">PART&nbsp;I.&#160; FINANCIAL INFORMATION</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Item 4.</font></u><b><font style="font-weight:bold;">&#160; </font></b><u>Controls and Procedures</u></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(a)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i><font style="font-style:italic;">Evaluation
of disclosure controls and procedures.&#160; </font></i>The Chief Executive Officer,
Miles D. White, and Chief Financial Officer, Thomas C. Freyman, evaluated the
effectiveness of Abbott Laboratories&#146; disclosure controls and procedures as of
the end of the period covered by this report, and concluded that Abbott
Laboratories&#146; disclosure controls and procedures were effective to ensure that
information Abbott is required to disclose in the reports that it files or
submits with the Securities and Exchange Commission under the Securities
Exchange Act of 1934 (the &#147;Exchange Act&#148;) is recorded, processed, summarized
and reported, within the time periods specified in the Commission&#146;s rules&nbsp;and
forms, and to ensure that information required to be disclosed by Abbott in the
reports that it files or submits under the Exchange Act is accumulated and
communicated to Abbott&#146;s management, including its principal executive officer
and principal financial officer, as appropriate to allow timely decisions
regarding required disclosure.</p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(b)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i><font style="font-style:italic;">Changes in
internal control over financial reporting.</font></i>&#160; Abbott is in the
process of implementing certain modules of an enterprise resource planning
system.&#160; In the third quarter of 2005,
the company implemented the Financial Accounting, Controlling, and the
Purchasing portion of the Materials Management modules of this system for
corporate headquarters.&#160; During the
quarter ended September&nbsp;30, 2005, there were no other changes in Abbott&#146;s
internal control over financial reporting (as defined in Rule&nbsp;13a-15(f)&nbsp;under
the Exchange Act) that have materially affected, or are reasonably likely to
materially affect, Abbott&#146;s internal control over financial reporting.</p>

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">19</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">PART&nbsp;II.&#160;&#160;&#160; OTHER INFORMATION</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Item 1.</font></u><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><u>Legal
Proceedings</u></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott is
involved in various claims, legal proceedings and investigations, including (as
of September&nbsp;30, 2005, except as otherwise indicated) those described
below.</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In its Form&nbsp;10-Q
for the second quarter of 2005, Abbott reported that a number of cases, brought
as purported class actions or representative actions, are pending that allege
generally that Abbott and numerous other pharmaceutical companies reported
false pricing information in connection with certain drugs that are
reimbursable under Medicare and Medicaid.&#160;
These cases brought by private plaintiffs, state counties and State
Attorneys General generally seek damages, treble damages, disgorgement of profits,
restitution and attorneys&#146; fees.&#160; The
federal court cases have been consolidated in the United States District Court
for the District of Massachusetts as <i><font style="font-style:italic;">In
re:&#160;&#160; Pharmaceutical Industry Average
Wholesale Price Litigation, MDL 1456.</font></i>&#160; During the third quarter, six additional New
York counties filed lawsuits in federal court in New York that have been or
will be transferred to <i><font style="font-style:italic;">MDL 1456.&#160; </font></i>One previously reported case, <i><font style="font-style:italic;">County of Erie, </font></i>has now been transferred
to <i><font style="font-style:italic;">MDL 1456.&#160;
</font></i>In addition, two cases were removed to federal court:&#160; <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Commonwealth
of Kentucky ex rel. Albert B. Chandler III, Attorney General </font></i>and <i><font style="font-style:italic;">State of Illinois</font></i>.</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In its Form&nbsp;10-Q
for the second quarter of 2005, Abbott reported that ten lawsuits, including
nine purported class actions, were pending against Abbott, Fournier Industrie
et Sante, and Laboratoires Fournier, S.A. (Fournier) in the United States
District Court for the District of Delaware alleging antitrust and unfair
competition claims in connection with the sale of fenofibrate
formulations.&#160; During the third quarter,
four additional lawsuits, including two purported class actions, were filed in
the United States District Court for the District of Delaware.&#160; The two purported class actions are
captioned: <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Philadelphia Federation of
Teachers Health and Welfare Fund </font></i>and <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Cindy Cronin, </font></i>and were filed in July&nbsp;2005.&#160; The two individual lawsuits are
captioned:&#160; <i><font style="font-style:italic;">CVS Pharmacy,&nbsp;Inc., Rite Aid Corporation, Rite Aid Headquarters
Corp.</font></i> and<i><font style="font-style:italic;"> Pacificare Health
Systems,&nbsp;Inc., </font></i>and were filed in August&nbsp;2005<i><font style="font-style:italic;">.&#160; </font></i>These
cases seek damages, treble damages and other relief.</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In its Form&nbsp;10-Q
for the second quarter of 2005, Abbott reported that it is a defendant in
numerous lawsuits involving the drug oxycodone, a drug manufactured and sold by
Purdue Pharma under the trademark OxyContin&#174;.&#160;
Abbott promoted OxyContin to certain specialty physicians, including
surgeons and anesthesiologists, under a co-promotion agreement with Purdue
Pharma.&#160; Most of the lawsuits allege
generally that plaintiffs suffered personal injuries as a result of taking
OxyContin.&#160; A few lawsuits allege
consumer protection violations and unfair trade practices. One suit by a third
party payor alleges antitrust pricing violations and overpricing of the drug.
As of September&nbsp;30, 2005, a total of 195 lawsuits are pending in which
Abbott is a party, of which 19 cases are pending in federal court and 176 cases
are pending in state court.&#160; 185 cases
are brought by individual plaintiffs, and 10 cases are brought as purported
class action lawsuits.&#160; Purdue Pharma is
a defendant in each lawsuit and, pursuant to the co-promotion agreement, Purdue
is required to indemnify Abbott in each lawsuit.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">20</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In its Form&nbsp;10-Q
for the second quarter of 2005, Abbott reported that it was involved in five
cases pending in the United States District Court for the Northern District of
Illinois related to Abbott&#146;s patents for clarithromycin (a drug Abbott sells
under the trademarks Biaxin&#174;, Biaxin&#174;XL, Klacid&#174;, and Klaricid&#174;).&#160; In September&nbsp;2005, Abbott filed patent
infringement claims against Sandoz,&nbsp;Inc. (&#147;Sandoz&#148;) in the United States
District Court for the Northern District of Illinois regarding its proposed
generic clarithromycin products.&#160; Abbott
will seek a preliminary injunction preventing Sandoz from marketing its
infringing generic product.&#160; Abbott has
resolved the previously reported litigation in the Netherlands, Ireland and
Belgium.</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In its Form&nbsp;10-Q
for the second quarter of 2005, Abbott reported that five cases are pending
related to Abbott&#146;s patents for sevoflurane (an anesthesia product Abbott sells
under the trademarks Ultane and Sevorane&#174;).&#160;
In one of the two cases pending in the United States District Court for
the Northern District of Illinois against Baxter Healthcare Corporation, the
Court issued a decision ruling that Abbott&#146;s patent is valid but that Baxter&#146;s
product does not infringe Abbott&#146;s patent.&#160;
Abbott has appealed that decision.</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As
reported in Abbott&#146;s 2004 Form&nbsp;10-K, Abbott is a defendant in several
lawsuits pending in the United States District Court for the District of
Minnesota and consolidated under the caption <i><font style="font-style:italic;">In
re: Canadian Import Antitrust Litigation </font></i>alleging generally that
Abbott and numerous other pharmaceutical manufacturers violated antitrust laws
by conspiring to prevent re-importation of drugs from Canada.&#160; In August&nbsp;2005, the court dismissed with
prejudice plaintiffs&#146; federal law claims, and dismissed without prejudice
plaintiffs&#146; state law claims.&#160; Plaintiffs
have filed a notice of appeal.</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">While it is not feasible to predict the outcome of such pending claims,
proceedings and investigations with certainty, management is of the opinion
that their ultimate dispositions should not have a material adverse effect on
Abbott&#146;s financial position, cash flows, or results of operations.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">21</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">NOTE:</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>For the purpose of calculating this ratio, (i)&nbsp;earnings
have been calculated by adjusting earnings from continuing operations for taxes
on earnings from continuing operations; interest expense; capitalized interest
cost, net of amortization; minority interest; and the portion of rentals
representative of the interest factor, (ii)&nbsp;Abbott considers one-third of
rental expense to be the amount representing return on capital, and (iii)&nbsp;fixed
charges comprise total interest expense, including capitalized interest and
such portion of rentals.</p>
